[Silesian](/wiki/Silesian_Voivodeship "Silesian Voivodeship") | _Śląskie_ | [Katowice](/wiki/Katowice "Katowice") | 12,333 | 4,492,330   
[Subcarpathian](/wiki/Subcarpathian_Voivodeship "Subcarpathian Voivodeship") | _Podkarpackie_ | [Rzeszów](/wiki/Rzesz%C3%B3w "Rzeszów") | 17,846 | 2,121,229   
[Holy Cross](/wiki/%C5%9Awi%C4%99tokrzyskie_Voivodeship "Świętokrzyskie Voivodeship") | _Świętokrzyskie_ | [Kielce](/wiki/Kielce "Kielce") | 11,710 | 1,224,626   
[Warmian-Masurian](/wiki/Warmian-Masurian_Voivodeship "Warmian-Masurian Voivodeship") | _Warmińsko-Mazurskie_ | [Olsztyn](/wiki/Olsztyn "Olsztyn") | 24,173 | 1,416,495   
[West Pomeranian](/wiki/West_Pomeranian_Voivodeship "West Pomeranian Voivodeship") | _Zachodniopomorskie_ | [Szczecin](/wiki/Szczecin "Szczecin") | 22,905 | 1,688,047   
  
### Law

Main article: [Law of Poland](/wiki/Law_of_Poland "Law of Poland")

The [_Constitution of 3 May_](/wiki/Constitution_of_May_3,_1791 "Constitution of May 3, 1791") adopted in 1791 was the first modern constitution in Europe.

The [Constitution of Poland](/wiki/Constitution_of_Poland "Constitution of Poland") is the enacted supreme law, and Polish judicature is based on the principle of civil rights, governed by the code of [civil law](/wiki/Civil_law_\(legal_system\) "Civil law \(legal system\)").[211] The current [democratic](/wiki/Democracy "Democracy") constitution was adopted by the [National Assembly of Poland](/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Poland "National Assembly of Poland") on 2 April 1997; it guarantees a [multi-party state](/wiki/Multi-party_state "Multi-party state") with freedoms of religion, speech and assembly, prohibits the practices of forced [medical experimentation](/wiki/Medical_experimentation "Medical experimentation"), torture or [corporal punishment](/wiki/Corporal_punishment "Corporal punishment"), and acknowledges the inviolability of the home, the right to form [trade unions](/wiki/Trade_union "Trade union"), and the right to [strike](/wiki/Strike_action "Strike action").[212]

The [judiciary](/wiki/Judiciary "Judiciary") in Poland is composed of the [Supreme Court](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Poland "Supreme Court of Poland") as the country's highest judicial organ, the [Supreme Administrative Court](/wiki/Supreme_Administrative_Court_of_Poland "Supreme Administrative Court of Poland") for the judicial control of public administration, Common Courts ([District](/wiki/District_Court "District Court"), [Regional](/wiki/Regional_Court_\(Poland\) "Regional Court \(Poland\)"), [Appellate](/wiki/Appellate_court "Appellate court")) and the [Military Court](/wiki/Court-martial "Court-martial").[213] The [Constitutional](/wiki/Constitutional_Tribunal_\(Poland\) "Constitutional Tribunal \(Poland\)") and State Tribunals are separate judicial bodies, which rule the constitutional liability of people holding the highest offices of state and supervise the compliance of [statutory law](/wiki/Statutory_law "Statutory law"), thus protecting the Constitution.[214] Judges are nominated by the [National Council of the Judiciary](/wiki/National_Council_of_the_Judiciary "National Council of the Judiciary") and are appointed for life by the [president](/wiki/President_of_Poland "President of Poland").[214] On the approval of the Senate, the Sejm appoints an [ombudsman](/wiki/Ombudsman "Ombudsman") for a five-year term to guard the observance of social justice.[204]

Poland has a low [homicide](/wiki/Homicide "Homicide") rate at 0.7 murders per 100,000 people, as of 2018.[215] Rape, assault and violent crime remain at a very low level.[216] The country has imposed strict regulations on [abortion](/wiki/Abortion_in_Poland "Abortion in Poland"), which is permitted only in cases of rape, incest or when the woman's life is in danger; [congenital disorder](/wiki/Congenital_disorder "Congenital disorder") and [stillbirth](/wiki/Stillbirth "Stillbirth") are not covered by the law, prompting some women to seek abortion abroad.[217]

Historically, the most significant Polish legal act is the [Constitution of 3 May 1791](/wiki/Constitution_of_3_May_1791 "Constitution of 3 May 1791"). Instituted to redress long-standing political defects of the [federative](/wiki/Federation "Federation") [Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth](/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth "Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth") and its [Golden Liberty](/wiki/Golden_Liberty "Golden Liberty"), it was the first modern constitution in Europe and influenced many later [democratic movements](/wiki/Democratic_movement "Democratic movement") across the globe.[218][219][220] In 1918, the [Second Polish Republic](/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic "Second Polish Republic") became one of the first countries to introduce universal [women's suffrage](/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage "Women's suffrage").[221]

### Foreign relations

Main articles: [Foreign relations of Poland](/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Poland "Foreign relations of Poland") and [List of diplomatic missions of Poland](/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Poland "List of diplomatic missions of Poland")

The [Ministry of Foreign Affairs](/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_\(Poland\) "Ministry of Foreign Affairs \(Poland\)"), located in [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw")

Poland is a [middle power](/wiki/Middle_power "Middle power") and is transitioning into a [regional power](/wiki/Regional_power "Regional power") in Europe.[222][223] It has a total of 52 representatives in the [European Parliament](/wiki/European_Parliament "European Parliament") as of 2022.[224] [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw") serves as the headquarters for [Frontex](/wiki/Frontex "Frontex"), the European Union's agency for external border security as well as [ODIHR](/wiki/ODIHR "ODIHR"), one of the principal institutions of the [OSCE](/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe "Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe").[225][226] Apart from the European Union, Poland has been a member of [NATO](/wiki/NATO "NATO"), the [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"), and the [WTO](/wiki/World_Trade_Organization "World Trade Organization"). 

In recent years, Poland significantly strengthened its [relations](/wiki/Poland%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Poland–United States relations") with the United States, thus becoming one of its closest [allies](/wiki/Alliance "Alliance") and strategic partners in Europe.[227] Historically, Poland maintained strong [cultural and political](/wiki/Hungary%E2%80%93Poland_relations "Hungary–Poland relations") ties to Hungary; this special relationship was recognised by the parliaments of both countries in 2007 with the joint declaration of 23 March as "The Day of Polish-Hungarian Friendship".[228]

### Military

Main article: [Polish Armed Forces](/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces "Polish Armed Forces")

.jpg)[Polish Air Force](/wiki/Polish_Air_Force "Polish Air Force") [F-16s](/wiki/F-16_Fighting_Falcon "F-16 Fighting Falcon"), a single-engine [multirole](/wiki/Multirole_combat_aircraft "Multirole combat aircraft") [fighter aircraft](/wiki/Fighter_aircraft "Fighter aircraft")

The [Polish Armed Forces](/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces "Polish Armed Forces") are composed of five branches – the [Land Forces](/wiki/Polish_Land_Forces "Polish Land Forces"), the [Navy](/wiki/Polish_Navy "Polish Navy"), the [Air Force](/wiki/Polish_Air_Force "Polish Air Force"), the [Special Forces](/wiki/Special_forces_of_Poland "Special forces of Poland") and the [Territorial Defence Force](/wiki/Territorial_Defence_Force_\(Poland\) "Territorial Defence Force \(Poland\)").[229] The military is subordinate to the [Ministry of National Defence of the Republic of Poland](/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_of_the_Republic_of_Poland "Ministry of National Defence of the Republic of Poland").[229] However, its commander-in-chief in peacetime is the president, who nominates officers, the Minister for National Defence and the chief of staff.[229] Polish military tradition is generally commemorated by the [Armed Forces Day](/wiki/Armed_Forces_Day_\(Poland\) "Armed Forces Day \(Poland\)"), celebrated annually on 15 August.[230] As of 2022, the Polish Armed Forces have a combined strength of 114,050 active soldiers, with a further 75,400 active in the [gendarmerie](/wiki/Military_Gendarmerie_\(Poland\) "Military Gendarmerie \(Poland\)") and [defence force](/wiki/Home_guard "Home guard").[231]

Poland is spending 2% of its GDP on defence, equivalent to approximately US$14.5 billion in 2022, with a slated increase to US$29 billion in 2023.[232][233] From 2022, Poland is set to spend 110 billion euros on the modernisation of its armed forces, in close cooperation with American, South Korean and local Polish [defence manufacturers](/wiki/Arms_industry "Arms industry").[234] Also, the Polish military is set to increase its size to 250,000 enlisted and officers, and 50,000 defence force personnel.[235] According to [SIPRI](/wiki/SIPRI "SIPRI"), the country exported €487 million worth of arms and armaments to foreign countries in 2020.[236]

Compulsory [military service](/wiki/Conscription "Conscription") for men, who previously had to serve for nine months, was discontinued in 2008.[237] Polish military doctrine reflects the same defensive nature as that of its NATO partners and the country actively hosts NATO's [military exercises](/wiki/Military_exercises "Military exercises").[231] Since 1953, the country has been a large contributor to various [United Nations](/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations") peacekeeping missions,[238] and currently maintains military presence in the Middle East, Africa, the [Baltic states](/wiki/Baltic_states "Baltic states") and [southeastern Europe](/wiki/Southeastern_Europe "Southeastern Europe").[231]

### Security, law enforcement and emergency services

Main articles: [Law enforcement in Poland](/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Poland "Law enforcement in Poland"), [Emergency medical services in Poland](/wiki/Emergency_medical_services_in_Poland "Emergency medical services in Poland"), and [State Fire Service](/wiki/State_Fire_Service "State Fire Service")

A [Mercedes-Benz Sprinter](/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Sprinter "Mercedes-Benz Sprinter") patrol van belonging to the Polish [State Police Service](/wiki/Policja "Policja") ( _Policja_ )

Thanks to its location, Poland is a country free from objective threats such as [earthquakes](/wiki/Earthquakes "Earthquakes"), [volcanic eruptions](/wiki/Volcanic_eruptions "Volcanic eruptions"), [tornadoes](/wiki/Tornadoes "Tornadoes") and [tropical cyclones](/wiki/Tropical_cyclones "Tropical cyclones"). 

Law enforcement in Poland is performed by several agencies which are subordinate to the [Ministry of Interior and Administration](/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_and_Administration_\(Poland\) "Ministry of Interior and Administration \(Poland\)") – the [State Police](/wiki/Policja "Policja") ( _Policja_ ), assigned to investigate crimes or transgression; the [Municipal City Guard](/wiki/City_Guard_\(Poland\) "City Guard \(Poland\)"), which maintains public order; and several specialised agencies, such as the [Polish Border Guard](/wiki/Polish_Border_Guard "Polish Border Guard").[239] Private security firms are also common, although they possess no legal authority to arrest or detain a suspect.[239][240] Municipal guards are primarily headed by provincial, regional or city councils; individual guards are not permitted to carry [firearms](/wiki/Firearms "Firearms") unless instructed by the superior commanding officer.[241] Security service personnel conduct regular patrols in both large urban areas or smaller suburban localities.[242]

The [Internal Security Agency](/wiki/Internal_Security_Agency "Internal Security Agency") (ABW, or ISA in English) is the chief [counter-intelligence instrument](/wiki/Intelligence_agency "Intelligence agency") safeguarding Poland's internal security, along with [Agencja Wywiadu](/wiki/Agencja_Wywiadu "Agencja Wywiadu") (AW) which identifies threats and collects secret information abroad.[243] The [Central Investigation Bureau of Police](/wiki/Centralne_Biuro_%C5%9Aledcze_Policji "Centralne Biuro Śledcze Policji") (CBŚP) and the [Central Anticorruption Bureau](/wiki/Central_Anticorruption_Bureau "Central Anticorruption Bureau") (CBA) are responsible for countering organised crime and corruption in state and private institutions.[244][245]

Emergency services in Poland consist of the [emergency medical services](/wiki/Emergency_medical_services_in_Poland "Emergency medical services in Poland"), [search and rescue](/wiki/Search_and_rescue#Poland "Search and rescue") units of the [Polish Armed Forces](/wiki/Polish_Armed_Forces "Polish Armed Forces") and [State Fire Service](/wiki/State_Fire_Service "State Fire Service"). Emergency medical services in Poland are operated by local and regional governments,[246] but are a part of the centralised national agency – the [National Medical Emergency Service](/wiki/Emergency_medical_services_in_Poland "Emergency medical services in Poland") ( _Państwowe Ratownictwo Medyczne_ ).[247]

## Economy

Main article: [Economy of Poland](/wiki/Economy_of_Poland "Economy of Poland")



* * *

Economic indicators  
  
---  
[GDP (PPP)](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") | $1.705 trillion (2023) | [9]  
Nominal [GDP](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") | $748.8 billion (2023) | [9]  
Real GDP growth | 4.5% (2019) | [248]  
[CPI](/wiki/Consumer_price_index "Consumer price index") inflation | 2.2% (2019) | [249]  
[Employment-to-population ratio](/wiki/Employment-to-population_ratio "Employment-to-population ratio") | 55% (2019) | [250]  
[Unemployment](/wiki/Unemployment "Unemployment") | 2.9% (2021) | [251]  
[Total public debt](/wiki/National_debt "National debt") | $274 billion (2019) | [252]  
  
As of 2023, Poland's economy and [gross domestic product](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") (GDP) is the sixth largest in the European Union by [nominal standards](/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union "Economy of the European Union") and the fifth largest by [purchasing power parity](/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_in_Europe_by_GDP_\(PPP\) "List of sovereign states and dependent territories in Europe by GDP \(PPP\)"). It is also one of the fastest growing within the Union and reached a [developed market](/wiki/Developed_market "Developed market") status in 2018.[253] The unemployment rate published by [Eurostat](/wiki/Eurostat "Eurostat") in 2021 amounted to 2.9%, which was the second-lowest in the EU.[251] Around 61% of the employed population works in the [service sector](/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy "Tertiary sector of the economy"), 31% in manufacturing, and 8% in the [agricultural](/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture") sector.[254] Although Poland is a member of EU's [single market](/wiki/European_Single_Market "European Single Market"), the country has not adopted the [Euro](/wiki/Euro "Euro") as legal tender and maintains its own currency – the [Polish złoty](/wiki/Polish_z%C5%82oty "Polish złoty") (zł, PLN). 

Poland is the regional economic leader in [Central Europe](/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe"), with nearly 40 per cent of the 500 biggest companies in the region (by revenues) as well as a [high globalisation rate](/wiki/Globalisation_index "Globalisation index").[255] The country's largest firms compose the [WIG20](/wiki/WIG20 "WIG20") and [WIG30](/wiki/WIG30 "WIG30") [indexes](/wiki/Stock_market_index "Stock market index"), which is traded on the [Warsaw Stock Exchange](/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange "Warsaw Stock Exchange"). According to reports made by the [National Bank of Poland](/wiki/National_Bank_of_Poland "National Bank of Poland"), the value of Polish foreign direct investments reached almost 300 billion [PLN](/wiki/Polish_z%C5%82oty "Polish złoty") at the end of 2014. The [Central Statistical Office](/wiki/Central_Statistical_Office_\(Poland\) "Central Statistical Office \(Poland\)") estimated that in 2014 there were 1,437 Polish corporations with interests in 3,194 foreign entities.[256]

Poland has the largest banking sector in Central Europe,[257] with 32.3 branches per 100,000 adults.[258] It was the only European economy to have avoided the [recession of 2008](/wiki/Great_Recession "Great Recession").[259] The country is the [20th largest exporter](/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports "List of countries by exports") of goods and services in the world.[260] Exports of goods and services are valued at approximately 56% of GDP, as of 2020.[261] In 2019, Poland passed a law that would exempt workers under the age of 26 from [income tax](/wiki/Income_tax "Income tax").[262]

### Tourism

Main articles: [Tourism in Poland](/wiki/Tourism_in_Poland "Tourism in Poland"), [List of World Heritage Sites of Poland](/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_of_Poland "List of World Heritage Sites of Poland"), [List of Historic Monuments (Poland)](/wiki/List_of_Historic_Monuments_\(Poland\) "List of Historic Monuments \(Poland\)"), [Seven Wonders of Poland](/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_Poland "Seven Wonders of Poland"), and [Crown of Polish Mountains](/wiki/Crown_of_Polish_Mountains "Crown of Polish Mountains")

The [Old City of Zamość](/wiki/Zamo%C5%9B%C4%87 "Zamość") is a [UNESCO World Heritage Site](/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site").

Poland experienced a significant increase in the number of tourists after joining the European Union in 2004.[263][264] With nearly 21 million international arrivals in 2019, tourism contributes considerably to the overall economy and makes up a relatively large proportion of the country's service market.[265]

Tourist attractions in Poland vary, from the mountains in the south to the sandy beaches in the north, with a trail of nearly every architectural style. The most visited city is [Kraków](/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków"), which was the former capital of Poland and serves as a relic of the [Polish Golden Age](/wiki/Polish_Golden_Age "Polish Golden Age") and the [Renaissance](/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland "Renaissance in Poland"). Kraków also held [royal coronations](/wiki/Royal_coronations_in_Poland "Royal coronations in Poland") of [most Polish kings and monarchs](/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs "List of Polish monarchs") at [Wawel](/wiki/Wawel "Wawel"), the nation's chief historical landmark. Among other notable sites in the country is [Wrocław](/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw "Wrocław"), one of the oldest cities in Poland which was a model for the founding of Kraków. Wrocław is famous for its [dwarf statues](/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw%27s_dwarfs "Wrocław's dwarfs"), a large [market square](/wiki/Market_Square,_Wroc%C5%82aw "Market Square, Wrocław") with two [town halls](/wiki/Ratusz "Ratusz"), and the oldest [Zoological Gardens](/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Zoo "Wrocław Zoo") with one of the world's largest number of animal [species](/wiki/Species "Species"). The Polish capital [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw") and its historical [Old Town](/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town "Warsaw Old Town") were entirely reconstructed after [wartime destruction](/wiki/Destruction_of_Warsaw "Destruction of Warsaw"). Other cities attracting countless tourists include [Gdańsk](/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk "Gdańsk"), [Poznań](/wiki/Pozna%C5%84 "Poznań"), [Lublin](/wiki/Lublin "Lublin"), [Toruń](/wiki/Toru%C5%84 "Toruń") as well as the site of the [German](/wiki/Germany "Germany") [Auschwitz concentration camp](/wiki/Auschwitz_concentration_camp "Auschwitz concentration camp") in [Oświęcim](/wiki/O%C5%9Bwi%C4%99cim "Oświęcim"). A notable highlight is the 13th-century [Wieliczka Salt Mine](/wiki/Wieliczka_Salt_Mine "Wieliczka Salt Mine") with its labyrinthine tunnels, a [subterranean lake](/wiki/Underground_lake "Underground lake") and chapels carved by miners out of [rock salt](/wiki/Rock_salt "Rock salt") beneath the ground.[ _[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_ ]

Other tourist destinations include the [Baltic Sea](/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea") coast in the north; the [Masurian Lake District](/wiki/Masurian_Lake_District "Masurian Lake District") and [Białowieża Forest](/wiki/Bia%C5%82owie%C5%BCa_Forest "Białowieża Forest") in the east; on the south [Karkonosze](/wiki/Karkonosze "Karkonosze"), the [Table Mountains](/wiki/Table_Mountains "Table Mountains") and the [Tatra Mountains](/wiki/Tatra_Mountains "Tatra Mountains"), where [Rysy](/wiki/Rysy "Rysy") – the highest peak of Poland, and [Eagle's Path](/wiki/Orla_Per%C4%87 "Orla Perć") mountain trail are located. The [Pieniny](/wiki/Pieniny "Pieniny") and [Bieszczady Mountains](/wiki/Bieszczady_Mountains "Bieszczady Mountains") lie in the extreme south-east.[266] There are [over 100 castles](/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Poland "List of castles in Poland") in the country, most in the [Lower Silesian Voivodeship](/wiki/Lower_Silesian_Voivodeship "Lower Silesian Voivodeship"), and also on the [Trail of the Eagles' Nests](/wiki/Trail_of_the_Eagles%27_Nests "Trail of the Eagles' Nests").[267] The largest castle in the world by land area is situated in [Malbork](/wiki/Malbork_Castle "Malbork Castle"), in north-central Poland.[268]

### Transport

Main article: [Transport in Poland](/wiki/Transport_in_Poland "Transport in Poland")

_Lichen99.jpg)[PKP Intercity](/wiki/Polish_State_Railways "Polish State Railways") [Pendolino](/wiki/New_Pendolino "New Pendolino") at the [Wrocław railway station](/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_G%C5%82%C3%B3wny_railway_station "Wrocław Główny railway station")

Transport in Poland is provided by means of [rail](/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Poland "Rail transport in Poland"), [road](/wiki/Roads_and_expressways_in_Poland "Roads and expressways in Poland"), [marine shipping](/wiki/Polish_Merchant_Navy "Polish Merchant Navy") and [air travel](/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Poland "List of airports in Poland"). The country is part of EU's [Schengen Area](/wiki/Schengen_Area "Schengen Area") and is an important transport hub due to its strategic geographical position in [Central Europe](/wiki/Central_Europe "Central Europe").[269] Some of the longest European routes, including the [E30](/wiki/European_route_E30 "European route E30") and [E40](/wiki/European_route_E40 "European route E40"), run through Poland. The country has a good network of [highways](/wiki/Highways_in_Poland "Highways in Poland") comprising [express roads](/wiki/Limited-access_road "Limited-access road") and [motorways](/wiki/Controlled-access_highway "Controlled-access highway"). As of August 2023, Poland maintains nearly 5,000 km (3,100 mi) of highways in use.[270]

In 2017, the nation had 18,513 kilometres (11,503 mi) of railway track, the third longest in the European Union after Germany and France.[271] The [Polish State Railways](/wiki/Polish_State_Railways "Polish State Railways") (PKP) is the dominant railway operator, with certain major voivodeships or urban areas possessing their own [commuter](/wiki/Commuter_rail "Commuter rail") and [regional rail](/wiki/Regional_rail "Regional rail").[272] Poland has a number of international airports, the largest of which is [Warsaw Chopin Airport](/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport "Warsaw Chopin Airport").[273] It is the primary global hub for [LOT Polish Airlines](/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines "LOT Polish Airlines"), the country's [flag carrier](/wiki/Flag_carrier "Flag carrier").[274]

Seaports exist all along Poland's Baltic coast, with most freight operations using [Świnoujście](/wiki/Port_of_%C5%9Awinouj%C5%9Bcie "Port of Świnoujście"), [Police](/wiki/Port_of_Police "Port of Police"), [Szczecin](/wiki/Port_of_Szczecin "Port of Szczecin"), [Kołobrzeg](/wiki/Port_of_Ko%C5%82obrzeg "Port of Kołobrzeg"), [Gdynia](/wiki/Port_of_Gdynia "Port of Gdynia"), [Gdańsk](/wiki/Port_of_Gda%C5%84sk "Port of Gdańsk") and [Elbląg](/wiki/Elbl%C4%85g "Elbląg") as their base. The [Port of Gdańsk](/wiki/Port_of_Gda%C5%84sk "Port of Gdańsk") is the only port in the [Baltic Sea](/wiki/Baltic_Sea "Baltic Sea") adapted to receive oceanic vessels. [Polferries](/wiki/Polferries "Polferries") and [Unity Line](/wiki/Unity_Line "Unity Line") are the largest Polish ferry operators, with the latter providing [roll-on/roll-off](/wiki/Roll-on/roll-off "Roll-on/roll-off") and [train ferry](/wiki/Train_ferry "Train ferry") services to [Scandinavia](/wiki/Scandinavia "Scandinavia").[275]

### Energy

Main article: [Energy in Poland](/wiki/Energy_in_Poland "Energy in Poland")

The electricity generation sector in Poland is largely [fossil-fuel](/wiki/Fossil_fuel "Fossil fuel")–based. [Coal](/wiki/Coal "Coal") production in Poland is a major source of employment and the largest source of the nation's [greenhouse gas emissions](/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions "Greenhouse gas emissions").[276] Many power plants nationwide use Poland's position as a major European exporter of coal to their advantage by continuing to use coal as the primary raw material in the production of their energy. The three largest Polish coal mining firms ([Węglokoks](/wiki/W%C4%99glokoks "Węglokoks"), [Kompania Węglowa](/wiki/Kompania_W%C4%99glowa "Kompania Węglowa") and [JSW](/wiki/Jastrz%C4%99bska_Sp%C3%B3%C5%82ka_W%C4%99glowa "Jastrzębska Spółka Węglowa")) extract around 100 million tonnes of coal annually.[277] After coal, Polish energy supply relies significantly on oil—the nation is the third-largest buyer of Russian oil exports to the EU.[278]

The new [Energy Policy of Poland until 2040](/wiki/Energy_in_Poland "Energy in Poland") (EPP2040) would reduce the share of coal and [lignite](/wiki/Lignite "Lignite") in electricity generation by 25% from 2017 to 2030. The plan involves deploying new nuclear plants, increasing energy efficiency, and decarbonising the Polish transport system in order to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and prioritise long-term energy security.[276][279]

### Science and technology

Main articles: [Polish science and technology](/wiki/Polish_science_and_technology "Polish science and technology") and [Polish people § Science and technology](/wiki/Polish_people#Science_and_technology "Polish people")

Physicist and chemist [Maria Skłodowska-Curie](/wiki/Marie_Curie "Marie Curie") was the first person to win two [Nobel Prizes](/wiki/Nobel_Prize "Nobel Prize").[280]

Over the course of history, the Polish people have made considerable contributions in the fields of science, technology and mathematics.[281] Perhaps the most renowned Pole to support this theory was [Nicolaus Copernicus](/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus "Nicolaus Copernicus") ( _Mikołaj Kopernik_ ), who triggered the [Copernican Revolution](/wiki/Copernican_Revolution "Copernican Revolution") by placing the [Sun rather than the Earth at the center of the universe](/wiki/Heliocentrism "Heliocentrism").[282] He also derived a [quantity theory of money](/wiki/Quantity_theory_of_money "Quantity theory of money"), which made him a pioneer of economics. Copernicus' achievements and discoveries are considered the basis of Polish culture and cultural identity.[283] Poland was ranked 41st in the [Global Innovation Index](/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index") in 2023.[284]

[Nicolaus Copernicus](/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus "Nicolaus Copernicus"), the 16th century Polish astronomer who formulated the [heliocentric](/wiki/Heliocentrism "Heliocentrism") model of the solar system

Poland's tertiary education institutions; traditional [universities](/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Poland "List of universities in Poland"), as well as technical, medical, and economic institutions, employ around tens of thousands of researchers and staff members. There are hundreds of research and development institutes.[285] However, in the 19th and 20th centuries many Polish scientists worked abroad; one of the most important of these exiles was [Maria Skłodowska-Curie](/wiki/Maria_Sk%C5%82odowska-Curie "Maria Skłodowska-Curie"), a physicist and chemist who lived much of her life in France. In 1925, she established Poland's [Radium Institute](/wiki/Curie_Institute_\(Warsaw\) "Curie Institute \(Warsaw\)").[280]

In the first half of the 20th century, Poland was a flourishing centre of mathematics. Outstanding Polish mathematicians formed the [Lwów School of Mathematics](/wiki/Lw%C3%B3w_School_of_Mathematics "Lwów School of Mathematics") (with [Stefan Banach](/wiki/Stefan_Banach "Stefan Banach"), [Stanisław Mazur](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Mazur "Stanisław Mazur"), [Hugo Steinhaus](/wiki/Hugo_Steinhaus "Hugo Steinhaus"), [Stanisław Ulam](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Ulam "Stanisław Ulam")) and [Warsaw School of Mathematics](/wiki/Warsaw_School_of_Mathematics "Warsaw School of Mathematics") (with [Alfred Tarski](/wiki/Alfred_Tarski "Alfred Tarski"), [Kazimierz Kuratowski](/wiki/Kazimierz_Kuratowski "Kazimierz Kuratowski"), [Wacław Sierpiński](/wiki/Wac%C5%82aw_Sierpi%C5%84ski "Wacław Sierpiński") and [Antoni Zygmund](/wiki/Antoni_Zygmund "Antoni Zygmund")). Numerous mathematicians, scientists, chemists or economists emigrated due to historic vicissitudes, among them [Benoit Mandelbrot](/wiki/Benoit_Mandelbrot "Benoit Mandelbrot"), [Leonid Hurwicz](/wiki/Leonid_Hurwicz "Leonid Hurwicz"), [Alfred Tarski](/wiki/Alfred_Tarski "Alfred Tarski"), [Joseph Rotblat](/wiki/Joseph_Rotblat "Joseph Rotblat") and [Nobel Prize](/wiki/Nobel_Prize "Nobel Prize") laureates [Roald Hoffmann](/wiki/Roald_Hoffmann "Roald Hoffmann"), [Georges Charpak](/wiki/Georges_Charpak "Georges Charpak") and [Tadeusz Reichstein](/wiki/Tadeusz_Reichstein "Tadeusz Reichstein"). 

## Demographics

Main articles: [Demographics of Poland](/wiki/Demographics_of_Poland "Demographics of Poland"), [List of cities and towns in Poland](/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Poland "List of cities and towns in Poland"), [Metropolitan areas in Poland](/wiki/Metropolitan_areas_in_Poland "Metropolitan areas in Poland"), [Polish people](/wiki/Polish_people "Polish people"), and [Polish diaspora](/wiki/Polish_diaspora "Polish diaspora")

Poland has a population of approximately 38.2 million as of 2021, and is the [ninth-most populous country](/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population "List of European countries by population") in Europe, as well as the fifth-most populous member state of the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union").[286] It has a population density of 122 inhabitants per square kilometre (320 inhabitants/sq mi).[287] The [total fertility rate](/wiki/Total_fertility_rate "Total fertility rate") was estimated at 1.42 children born to a woman in 2019, which is [among the world's lowest](/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependencies_by_total_fertility_rate "List of sovereign states and dependencies by total fertility rate").[288] Furthermore, Poland's population is [aging significantly](/wiki/List_of_countries_by_median_age "List of countries by median age"), and the country has a [median age](/wiki/Median_age "Median age") of roughly 42.[289]

Population of Poland from 1900 to 2010 in millions of inhabitants

Around 60% of the country's population lives in urban areas or major cities and 40% in rural zones.[290] In 2020, 50.2% of Poles resided in [detached dwellings](/wiki/Detached_dwelling "Detached dwelling") and 44.3% in [apartments](/wiki/Apartment "Apartment").[291] The most populous administrative province or state is the [Masovian Voivodeship](/wiki/Masovian_Voivodeship "Masovian Voivodeship") and the most populous city is the capital, [Warsaw](/wiki/Warsaw "Warsaw"), at 1.8 million inhabitants with a further 2–3 million people living in its [metropolitan area](/wiki/Warsaw_metropolitan_area "Warsaw metropolitan area").[292][293][294] The [metropolitan area](/wiki/Katowice_urban_area "Katowice urban area") of [Katowice](/wiki/Katowice "Katowice") is the largest urban [conurbation](/wiki/Conurbation "Conurbation") with a population between 2.7 million[295] and 5.3 million residents.[296] Population density is higher in the south of Poland and mostly concentrated between the cities of [Wrocław](/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw "Wrocław") and [Kraków](/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków").[297]

In the [2011 Polish census](/wiki/Polish_census_of_2011 "Polish census of 2011"), 37,310,341 people reported [Polish](/wiki/Polish_people "Polish people") identity, 846,719 [Silesian](/wiki/Silesians "Silesians"), 232,547 [Kashubian](/wiki/Kashubians "Kashubians") and 147,814 [German](/wiki/German_minority_in_Poland "German minority in Poland"). Other [identities](/wiki/Polish_people#National_minorities "Polish people") were reported by 163,363 people (0.41%) and 521,470 people (1.35%) did not specify any nationality.[2] Official population statistics do not include migrant workers who do not possess a permanent residency permit or [Karta Polaka](/wiki/Karta_Polaka "Karta Polaka").[298] More than 1.7 million [Ukrainian](/wiki/Ukrainians "Ukrainians") citizens worked legally in Poland in 2017.[299] The number of migrants is rising steadily; the country approved 504,172 work permits for foreigners in 2021 alone.[300]
