### Languages

Main articles: [Polish language](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language"), [Languages of Poland](/wiki/Languages_of_Poland "Languages of Poland"), and [Bilingual communes in Poland](/wiki/Bilingual_communes_in_Poland "Bilingual communes in Poland")

_Dolina Jadwigi_ —a [bilingual](/wiki/Bilingual "Bilingual") Polish-[Kashubian](/wiki/Kashubian_language "Kashubian language") road sign with the village name

[Polish](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language") is the [official](/wiki/Official_language "Official language") and predominant spoken language in Poland, and is one of the official [languages of the European Union](/wiki/Languages_of_the_European_Union "Languages of the European Union").[303] It is also a [second language](/wiki/Second_language "Second language") in parts of neighbouring [Lithuania](/wiki/Lithuania "Lithuania"), where it is taught in Polish-minority schools.[304][305] Contemporary Poland is a linguistically [homogeneous](/wiki/Homogeneous "Homogeneous") nation, with 97% of respondents declaring Polish as their mother tongue.[306] There are currently 15 minority languages in Poland,[307] including one recognised regional language, [Kashubian](/wiki/Kashubian_language "Kashubian language"), which is spoken by approximately 100,000 people on a daily basis in the northern regions of [Kashubia](/wiki/Kashubia "Kashubia") and [Pomerania](/wiki/Pomerania "Pomerania").[308] Poland also recognises [secondary administrative languages or auxiliary languages in bilingual municipalities](/wiki/Bilingual_communes_in_Poland "Bilingual communes in Poland"), where bilingual signs and placenames are commonplace.[309] According to the [Centre for Public Opinion Research](/wiki/Centre_for_Public_Opinion_Research "Centre for Public Opinion Research"), around 32% of Polish citizens declared knowledge of the [English language](/wiki/English_language "English language") in 2015.[310]

### Religion

Main article: [Religion in Poland](/wiki/Religion_in_Poland "Religion in Poland")

[John Paul II](/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II "Pope John Paul II"), born Karol Wojtyła, held the papacy between 1978–2005 and was the first [Pole](/wiki/Polish_people "Polish people") to become a [Roman Catholic](/wiki/Roman_Catholic "Roman Catholic") [Pope](/wiki/Pope "Pope").

According to the 2021 census, 71.3% of all Polish citizens adhere to the [Roman Catholic Church](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church_in_Poland "Roman Catholic Church in Poland"), with 6.9% identifying as having no religion and 20.6% refusing to answer.[311]

Poland is one of the [most religious countries in Europe](/wiki/Religion_in_Europe "Religion in Europe"), where Roman Catholicism remains a criterion of national identity and Polish-born [Pope John Paul II](/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II "Pope John Paul II") is widely revered.[312][313] In 2015, 61.6% of respondents outlined that religion is of high or very high importance.[314] However, church attendance has greatly decreased in recent years; only 28% of Catholics attended [mass](/wiki/Mass_\(liturgy\) "Mass \(liturgy\)") weekly in 2021, down from around half in 2000.[315] According to _[The Wall Street Journal](/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal "The Wall Street Journal")_ , "Of [the] more than 100 countries studied by the _[Pew Research Center](/wiki/Pew_Research_Center "Pew Research Center")_ in 2018, Poland was [secularizing](/wiki/Secularization "Secularization") the fastest, as measured by the disparity between the religiosity of young people and their elders."[312]

Freedom of religion in Poland is guaranteed by the Constitution, and Poland's [concordat](/wiki/Concordat "Concordat") with the [Holy See](/wiki/Holy_See "Holy See") enables the teaching of religion in public schools.[316] Historically, the Polish state maintained a high degree of [religious tolerance](/wiki/Warsaw_Confederation "Warsaw Confederation") and provided asylum for refugees fleeing religious persecution in other parts of Europe.[317] Poland hosted Europe's largest [Jewish diaspora](/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland "History of the Jews in Poland"), and the country was a centre of [Ashkenazi Jewish](/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jewish "Ashkenazi Jewish") culture and traditional learning until the [Holocaust](/wiki/The_Holocaust "The Holocaust").[318]

Contemporary religious minorities include [Orthodox Christians](/wiki/Polish_Orthodox_Church "Polish Orthodox Church"), [Protestants](/wiki/Protestants "Protestants")—including [Lutherans](/wiki/Lutherans "Lutherans") of the [Evangelical-Augsburg Church](/wiki/Evangelical-Augsburg_Church_in_Poland "Evangelical-Augsburg Church in Poland"), [Pentecostals](/wiki/Pentecostalism "Pentecostalism") in the [Pentecostal Church in Poland](/wiki/Pentecostal_Church_in_Poland "Pentecostal Church in Poland"), [Adventists](/wiki/Adventists "Adventists") in the [Seventh-day Adventist Church](/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church "Seventh-day Adventist Church"), and other smaller [Evangelical](/wiki/Evangelicalism "Evangelicalism") denominations—[Jehovah's Witnesses](/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses "Jehovah's Witnesses"), [Eastern Catholics](/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches "Eastern Catholic Churches"), [Mariavites](/wiki/Mariavite_Church "Mariavite Church"), [Jews](/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland "History of the Jews in Poland"), [Muslims](/wiki/Islam_in_Poland "Islam in Poland") ([Tatars](/wiki/Tatars "Tatars")), and [neopagans](/wiki/Modern_Paganism "Modern Paganism"), some of whom are members of the [Native Polish Church](/wiki/Native_Polish_Church "Native Polish Church").[319]

[Pilgrimages](/wiki/Pilgrimage "Pilgrimage") to the [Jasna Góra Monastery](/wiki/Jasna_G%C3%B3ra_Monastery "Jasna Góra Monastery"), a shrine [dedicated](/wiki/The_Most_Holy_Virgin_Mary,_Queen_of_Poland#History "The Most Holy Virgin Mary, Queen of Poland") to the [Black Madonna](/wiki/Black_Madonna_of_Cz%C4%99stochowa "Black Madonna of Częstochowa"), take place annually.[320]

### Health

Main article: [Health in Poland](/wiki/Health_in_Poland "Health in Poland")

Medical service providers and [hospitals](/wiki/Hospitals "Hospitals") ( _szpitale_ ) in Poland are subordinate to the [Ministry of Health](/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_of_the_Republic_of_Poland "Ministry of Health of the Republic of Poland"); it provides administrative oversight and scrutiny of general medical practice, and is obliged to maintain a high standard of [hygiene](/wiki/Hygiene "Hygiene") and patient care. Poland has a [universal healthcare system](/wiki/Universal_health_care "Universal health care") based on an all-inclusive [insurance system](/wiki/Health_insurance "Health insurance"); state subsidised healthcare is available to all citizens covered by the general health insurance program of the [National Health Fund](/wiki/National_Health_Fund "National Health Fund") (NFZ). Private medical complexes exist nationwide; over 50% of the population uses both public and private sectors.[321][322][323]

According to the [Human Development Report](/wiki/HDI "HDI") from 2020, the average life expectancy at birth is 79 years (around 75 years for an infant male and 83 years for an infant female);[324] the country has a low [infant mortality rate](/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate "Infant mortality rate") (4 per 1,000 births).[325] In 2019, the principal cause of death was [ischemic heart disease](/wiki/Ischemic_heart_disease "Ischemic heart disease"); diseases of the [circulatory system](/wiki/Circulatory_system "Circulatory system") accounted for 45% of all deaths.[326][327] In the same year, Poland was also the 15th-largest importer of [medications](/wiki/Medications "Medications") and pharmaceutical products.[328]

### Education

Main articles: [Education in Poland](/wiki/Education_in_Poland "Education in Poland") and [Universities in Poland](/wiki/Universities_in_Poland "Universities in Poland")

[Jagiellonian University](/wiki/Jagiellonian_University "Jagiellonian University") in [Kraków](/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków")

The [Jagiellonian University](/wiki/Jagiellonian_University "Jagiellonian University") founded in 1364 by [Casimir III](/wiki/Casimir_III_the_Great "Casimir III the Great") in [Kraków](/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków") was the first institution of higher learning established in Poland, and is one of the [oldest universities](/wiki/List_of_oldest_universities_in_continuous_operation "List of oldest universities in continuous operation") still in continuous operation.[329] Poland's [Commission of National Education](/wiki/Commission_of_National_Education "Commission of National Education") ( _Komisja Edukacji Narodowej_ ), established in 1773, was the world's first state ministry of education.[330][331]

The framework for [primary](/wiki/Primary_education "Primary education"), [secondary](/wiki/Secondary_education "Secondary education") and [higher](/wiki/Higher_education "Higher education") [tertiary education](/wiki/Tertiary_education "Tertiary education") are established by the [Ministry of Education and Science](/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Education_\(Poland\) "Ministry of National Education \(Poland\)"). Kindergarten attendance is optional for children aged between three and five, with one year being [compulsory](/wiki/Compulsory_education "Compulsory education") for six-year-olds.[332][333] Primary education traditionally begins at the age of seven, although children aged six can attend at the request of their parents or guardians.[333] Elementary school spans eight grades and secondary schooling is dependent on student preference – a four-year high school ( _[liceum](/wiki/General_education_liceum "General education liceum")_ ), a five-year technical school ( _[technikum](/wiki/Technikum_\(Polish_education\) "Technikum \(Polish education\)")_ ) or various [vocational studies](/wiki/Vocational_school "Vocational school") ( _szkoła branżowa_ ) can be pursued by each individual pupil.[333] A liceum or technikum is concluded with a maturity exit exam ( _[matura](/wiki/Matura "Matura")_ ), which must be passed in order to apply for a university or other institutions of higher learning.[334]

In Poland, there are over 500 university-level institutions,[335] with technical, medical, economic, agricultural, pedagogical, theological, musical, maritime and military faculties.[336] The [University of Warsaw](/wiki/University_of_Warsaw "University of Warsaw") and [Warsaw Polytechnic](/wiki/Warsaw_Polytechnic "Warsaw Polytechnic"), the [University of Wrocław](/wiki/University_of_Wroc%C5%82aw "University of Wrocław"), [Adam Mickiewicz University in Poznań](/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz_University_in_Pozna%C5%84 "Adam Mickiewicz University in Poznań") and the [University of Technology in Gdańsk](/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk_University_of_Technology "Gdańsk University of Technology") are among the most prominent.[337] There are three conventional [academic degrees](/wiki/Academic_degree "Academic degree") in Poland – _[licencjat](/wiki/Licentiate_\(degree\) "Licentiate \(degree\)")_ or _[inżynier](/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree "Bachelor's degree")_ (first cycle qualification), _[magister](/wiki/Magister_\(degree\) "Magister \(degree\)")_ (second cycle qualification) and _[doktor](/wiki/PhD "PhD")_ (third cycle qualification).[338] In 2018, the [Programme for International Student Assessment](/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment "Programme for International Student Assessment"), coordinated by the [Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development](/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development "Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development"), ranked Poland's educational system higher than the OECD average; the study showed that students in Poland perform better academically than in most OECD countries.[339]

## Culture

Main article: [Culture of Poland](/wiki/Culture_of_Poland "Culture of Poland")

The [Polish White Eagle](/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Poland "Coat of arms of Poland") is Poland's enduring [national and cultural symbol](/wiki/National_symbols_of_Poland "National symbols of Poland").

The culture of Poland is closely connected with its intricate 1,000-year [history](/wiki/History_of_Poland "History of Poland"), and forms an important constituent in the [Western civilisation](/wiki/Western_world "Western world").[340] The Poles take great pride in their national identity which is often associated with the colours white and red, and exuded by the expression _biało-czerwoni_ ("whitereds").[341] National symbols, chiefly the crowned [white-tailed eagle](/wiki/White-tailed_eagle "White-tailed eagle"), are often visible on clothing, insignia and emblems.[342] The architectural monuments of great importance are protected by the [National Heritage Board of Poland](/wiki/National_Heritage_Board_of_Poland "National Heritage Board of Poland").[343] Over 100 of the country's most significant tangible wonders were enlisted onto the [Historic Monuments Register](/wiki/List_of_Historic_Monuments_\(Poland\) "List of Historic Monuments \(Poland\)"),[344] with further 17 being recognised by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") as World Heritage Sites.[345]

### Holidays and traditions

See also: [Christmas in Poland](/wiki/Christmas_in_Poland "Christmas in Poland")

[All Saints' Day](/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day "All Saints' Day") on 1 November is one of the most important public holidays in Poland.

There are 13 government-approved annual public holidays – [New Year](/wiki/New_Year "New Year") on 1 January, [Three Kings' Day](/wiki/Epiphany_\(holiday\) "Epiphany \(holiday\)") on 6 January, [Easter Sunday](/wiki/Easter_Sunday "Easter Sunday") and [Easter Monday](/wiki/Easter_Monday "Easter Monday"), [Labour Day](/wiki/International_Workers%27_Day "International Workers' Day") on 1 May, [Constitution Day](/wiki/3_May_Constitution_Day "3 May Constitution Day") on 3 May, [Pentecost](/wiki/Pentecost "Pentecost"), [Corpus Christi](/wiki/Feast_of_Corpus_Christi "Feast of Corpus Christi"), [Feast of the Assumption](/wiki/Assumption_of_Mary "Assumption of Mary") on 15 August, [All Saints' Day](/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day "All Saints' Day") on 1 November, [Independence Day](/wiki/Independence_Day_\(Poland\) "Independence Day \(Poland\)") on 11 November and [Christmastide](/wiki/Christmas "Christmas") on 25 and 26 December.[346]

Particular traditions and superstitious customs observed in Poland are not found elsewhere in Europe. Though [Christmas Eve](/wiki/Christmas_Eve "Christmas Eve") ( _[Wigilia](/wiki/Wigilia "Wigilia")_ ) is not a public holiday, it remains the most memorable day of the entire year. [Trees](/wiki/Christmas_trees "Christmas trees") are decorated on 24 December, hay is placed under the tablecloth to resemble Jesus' [manger](/wiki/Manger "Manger"), [Christmas wafers](/wiki/Christmas_wafer "Christmas wafer") ( _opłatek_ ) are shared between gathered guests and a [twelve-dish meatless supper](/wiki/Twelve-dish_Christmas_Eve_supper "Twelve-dish Christmas Eve supper") is served that same evening when the [first star](/wiki/Star_of_Bethlehem "Star of Bethlehem") appears.[347] An empty plate and seat are symbolically left at the table for an unexpected guest.[348] On occasion, [carolers](/wiki/Christmas_carols "Christmas carols") journey around smaller towns with a folk [Turoń](/wiki/Turo%C5%84 "Turoń") creature until the [Lent](/wiki/Lent "Lent") period.[349]

A widely-popular [doughnut](/wiki/P%C4%85czki "Pączki") and sweet pastry feast occurs on [Fat Thursday](/wiki/Fat_Thursday "Fat Thursday"), usually 52 days prior to [Easter](/wiki/Easter "Easter").[350] [Eggs](/wiki/Easter_egg "Easter egg") for [Holy Sunday](/wiki/Easter_Sunday "Easter Sunday") are painted and placed in decorated [baskets](/wiki/%C5%9Awi%C4%99conka "Święconka") that are previously blessed by clergymen in churches on [Easter Saturday](/wiki/Easter_Saturday "Easter Saturday"). Easter Monday is celebrated with pagan _[dyngus](/wiki/%C5%9Amigus-dyngus "Śmigus-dyngus")_ festivities, where the youth is engaged in water fights.[351][350] Cemeteries and graves of the deceased are annually visited by family members on All Saints' Day; tombstones are cleaned as a sign of respect and candles are lit to honour the dead on an unprecedented scale.[352]

### Music

Main article: [Music of Poland](/wiki/Music_of_Poland "Music of Poland")

[![Fryderyk Chopin](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg/150px-Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg)](/wiki/File:Frederic_Chopin_photo.jpeg)

[Fryderyk Chopin](/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin "Frédéric Chopin") was a renowned classical composer and virtuoso pianist.

[![Artur Rubinstein](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Optreden_Arthur_Rubinstein_in_Concertgebouw%2C_Bestanddeelnr_913-5228.jpg/142px-Optreden_Arthur_Rubinstein_in_Concertgebouw%2C_Bestanddeelnr_913-5228.jpg)](/wiki/File:Optreden_Arthur_Rubinstein_in_Concertgebouw,_Bestanddeelnr_913-5228.jpg)

[Artur Rubinstein](/wiki/Arthur_Rubinstein "Arthur Rubinstein") was one of the greatest concert pianists of the 20th century.

Artists from Poland, including famous musicians such as [Frédéric Chopin](/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin "Frédéric Chopin"), [Artur Rubinstein](/wiki/Artur_Rubinstein "Artur Rubinstein"), [Ignacy Jan Paderewski](/wiki/Ignacy_Jan_Paderewski "Ignacy Jan Paderewski"), [Krzysztof Penderecki](/wiki/Krzysztof_Penderecki "Krzysztof Penderecki"), [Henryk Wieniawski](/wiki/Henryk_Wieniawski "Henryk Wieniawski"), [Karol Szymanowski](/wiki/Karol_Szymanowski "Karol Szymanowski"), and traditional, regionalised [folk composers](/wiki/Folk_music "Folk music") create a lively and diverse music scene, which even recognises its own music genres, such as [sung poetry](/wiki/Sung_poetry "Sung poetry") and [disco polo](/wiki/Disco_polo "Disco polo").[353]

The origins of Polish music can be traced to the 13th century; manuscripts have been found in [Stary Sącz](/wiki/Stary_S%C4%85cz "Stary Sącz") containing [polyphonic](/wiki/Polyphony "Polyphony") compositions related to the Parisian [Notre Dame School](/wiki/Notre_Dame_School "Notre Dame School"). Other early compositions, such as the melody of _[Bogurodzica](/wiki/Bogurodzica "Bogurodzica")_ and _[God Is Born](/wiki/God_Is_Born "God Is Born")_ (a coronation [polonaise tune](/wiki/Polonaise_\(dance\) "Polonaise \(dance\)") for Polish kings by an unknown composer), may also date back to this period, however, the first known notable composer, [Nicholas of Radom](/wiki/Miko%C5%82aj_z_Radomia "Mikołaj z Radomia"), lived in the 15th century. [Diomedes Cato](/wiki/Diomedes_Cato "Diomedes Cato"), a native-born Italian who lived in Kraków, became a renowned lutenist at the court of Sigismund III; he not only imported some of the musical styles from southern Europe but blended them with native folk music.[354]

In the 17th and 18th centuries, Polish baroque composers wrote [liturgical music](/wiki/Liturgical_music "Liturgical music") and secular compositions such as [concertos](/wiki/Concerto "Concerto") and [sonatas](/wiki/Sonata "Sonata") for voices or instruments. At the end of the 18th century, Polish classical music evolved into national forms like the [polonaise](/wiki/Polonaise_\(dance\) "Polonaise \(dance\)"). [Wojciech Bogusławski](/wiki/Wojciech_Bogus%C5%82awski "Wojciech Bogusławski") is accredited with composing the first Polish national [opera](/wiki/Opera "Opera"), titled _[Krakowiacy i Górale](https://pl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krakowiacy_i_G%C3%B3rale "pl:Krakowiacy i Górale")_ , which premiered in 1794.[355]

![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png)

**[Fryderyk Chopin](/wiki/Fryderyk_Chopin "Fryderyk Chopin")**

[Mazurka no. 4 in a minor, op. 17](/wiki/File:Frederic_Chopin_-_mazurka_no._4_in_a_minor,_op._17.ogg "File:Frederic Chopin - mazurka no. 4 in a minor, op. 17.ogg")

[Mazurka](/wiki/Mazurka "Mazurka") ([Polish](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language"): _mazurek_ ), stylised [folk dance](/wiki/Folk_dance "Folk dance") in [triple meter](/wiki/Triple_meter "Triple meter") (1832), commemorating the [November Uprising](/wiki/November_Uprising "November Uprising")

Poland today has an active music scene, with the jazz and metal genres being particularly popular among the contemporary populace. Polish jazz musicians such as [Krzysztof Komeda](/wiki/Krzysztof_Komeda "Krzysztof Komeda") created a unique style, which was most famous in the 1960s and 1970s and continues to be popular to this day. Poland has also become a major venue for large-scale music festivals, chief among which are the [Open'er Festival](/wiki/Open%27er_Festival "Open'er Festival"), [Opole Festival](/wiki/Opole_Festival "Opole Festival") and [Sopot Festival](/wiki/Sopot_Festival "Sopot Festival").[356]

### Art

Main articles: [Art in Poland](/wiki/Art_in_Poland "Art in Poland") and [Young Poland](/wiki/Young_Poland "Young Poland")

Further information: [List of Polish artists](/wiki/List_of_Polish_artists "List of Polish artists")

[![Jan Matejko](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Matejko_Self-portrait.jpg/140px-Matejko_Self-portrait.jpg)](/wiki/File:Matejko_Self-portrait.jpg)

[Jan Matejko](/wiki/Jan_Matejko "Jan Matejko"), leading Polish [history painter](/wiki/History_painting "History painting") whose works depict Poland's heritage and key historical events

[![Lady with an Ermine](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Lady_with_an_Ermine_-_Leonardo_da_Vinci_%28adjusted_levels%29.jpg/155px-Lady_with_an_Ermine_-_Leonardo_da_Vinci_%28adjusted_levels%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Lady_with_an_Ermine_-_Leonardo_da_Vinci_\(adjusted_levels\).jpg)

 _[Lady with an Ermine](/wiki/Lady_with_an_Ermine "Lady with an Ermine")_ (1490) by [Leonardo da Vinci](/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci "Leonardo da Vinci") is displayed in the [Czartoryski Museum](/wiki/Czartoryski_Museum "Czartoryski Museum") in Kraków.

Art in Poland has invariably reflected [European](/wiki/Art_of_Europe "Art of Europe") trends, with Polish painting pivoted on [folklore](/wiki/Folklore "Folklore"), [Catholic themes](/wiki/Catholic_art "Catholic art"), [historicism](/wiki/History_painting "History painting") and [realism](/wiki/Realism_\(arts\) "Realism \(arts\)"), but also on [impressionism](/wiki/Impressionism "Impressionism") and [romanticism](/wiki/Romanticism_in_Poland "Romanticism in Poland"). An important art movement was [Young Poland](/wiki/Young_Poland "Young Poland"), developed in the late 19th century for promoting [decadence](/wiki/Decadent_movement "Decadent movement"), [symbolism](/wiki/Symbolism_\(arts\) "Symbolism \(arts\)") and [art nouveau](/wiki/Art_nouveau "Art nouveau"). Since the 20th century Polish documentary art and photography has enjoyed worldwide fame, especially the [Polish School of Posters](/wiki/Polish_School_of_Posters "Polish School of Posters").[357] One of the most distinguished paintings in Poland is _[Lady with an Ermine](/wiki/Lady_with_an_Ermine "Lady with an Ermine")_ (1490) by [Leonardo da Vinci](/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci "Leonardo da Vinci").[358]

Internationally renowned Polish artists include [Jan Matejko](/wiki/Jan_Matejko "Jan Matejko") (historicism), [Jacek Malczewski](/wiki/Jacek_Malczewski "Jacek Malczewski") (symbolism), [Stanisław Wyspiański](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Wyspia%C5%84ski "Stanisław Wyspiański") (art nouveau), [Henryk Siemiradzki](/wiki/Henryk_Siemiradzki "Henryk Siemiradzki") (Roman [academic art](/wiki/Academic_art "Academic art")), [Tamara de Lempicka](/wiki/Tamara_de_Lempicka "Tamara de Lempicka") ([art deco](/wiki/Art_deco "Art deco")), and [Zdzisław Beksiński](/wiki/Zdzis%C5%82aw_Beksi%C5%84ski "Zdzisław Beksiński") (dystopian [surrealism](/wiki/Surrealism "Surrealism")).[359] Several Polish artists and sculptors were also acclaimed representatives of [avant-garde](/wiki/Avant-garde "Avant-garde"), [constructivist](/wiki/Constructivism_\(art\) "Constructivism \(art\)"), [minimalist](/wiki/Minimalism "Minimalism") and contemporary art movements, including [Katarzyna Kobro](/wiki/Katarzyna_Kobro "Katarzyna Kobro"), [Władysław Strzemiński](/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Strzemi%C5%84ski "Władysław Strzemiński"), [Magdalena Abakanowicz](/wiki/Magdalena_Abakanowicz "Magdalena Abakanowicz"), [Alina Szapocznikow](/wiki/Alina_Szapocznikow "Alina Szapocznikow"), [Igor Mitoraj](/wiki/Igor_Mitoraj "Igor Mitoraj") and [Wilhelm Sasnal](/wiki/Wilhelm_Sasnal "Wilhelm Sasnal"). 

Notable art academies in Poland include the [Kraków Academy of Fine Arts](/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w_Academy_of_Fine_Arts "Kraków Academy of Fine Arts"), [Academy of Fine Arts in Warsaw](/wiki/Academy_of_Fine_Arts_in_Warsaw "Academy of Fine Arts in Warsaw"), [Art Academy of Szczecin](/wiki/Art_Academy_of_Szczecin "Art Academy of Szczecin"), [University of Fine Arts in Poznań](/wiki/University_of_Fine_Arts_in_Pozna%C5%84 "University of Fine Arts in Poznań") and the [Geppert Academy of Fine Arts in Wrocław](/wiki/Eugeniusz_Geppert_Academy_of_Fine_Arts "Eugeniusz Geppert Academy of Fine Arts"). Contemporary works are exhibited at [Zachęta](/wiki/Zach%C4%99ta "Zachęta"), [Ujazdów](/wiki/Ujazd%C3%B3w_Castle "Ujazdów Castle"), and [MOCAK](/wiki/MOCAK,_Museum_of_Contemporary_Art_in_Krak%C3%B3w "MOCAK, Museum of Contemporary Art in Kraków") art galleries.[360]

### Architecture

Main article: [Architecture of Poland](/wiki/Architecture_of_Poland "Architecture of Poland")

[![Saint Mary's Church in Kraków](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/St_Mary%27s_Krakow.jpg/152px-St_Mary%27s_Krakow.jpg)](/wiki/File:St_Mary%27s_Krakow.jpg)

[St. Mary's Basilica](/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w "St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków") on the [Main Market Square](/wiki/Main_Market_Square,_Krak%C3%B3w "Main Market Square, Kraków") in [Kraków](/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w "Kraków") is an example of [Brick Gothic](/wiki/Brick_Gothic "Brick Gothic") architecture.

[![Poznań City Hall](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg/133px-Ayuntamiento%2C_Poznan%2C_Polonia%2C_2014-09-18%2C_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ayuntamiento,_Poznan,_Polonia,_2014-09-18,_DD_67-72_HDR.jpg)

The 16th-century [City Hall](/wiki/Pozna%C5%84_Town_Hall "Poznań Town Hall") of [Poznań](/wiki/Pozna%C5%84 "Poznań") illustrates the [Renaissance](/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland "Renaissance in Poland") style.

The [architecture of Poland](/wiki/Architecture_of_Poland "Architecture of Poland") reflects [European architectural](/wiki/Architecture_of_Europe "Architecture of Europe") styles, with strong historical influences derived from [Italy](/wiki/Architecture_of_Italy "Architecture of Italy"), [Germany](/wiki/Architecture_of_Germany "Architecture of Germany"), and the [Low Countries](/wiki/Low_Countries "Low Countries").[361] Settlements founded on [Magdeburg Law](/wiki/Magdeburg_rights "Magdeburg rights") evolved around [central marketplaces](/wiki/Town_square "Town square") ( _plac_ , _rynek_ ), encircled by a grid or [concentric](/wiki/Concentric_objects "Concentric objects") network of streets forming an [old town](/wiki/Old_town "Old town") ( _stare miasto_ ).[362] Poland's traditional landscape is characterised by ornate churches, [city tenements](/wiki/Kamienica_\(architecture\) "Kamienica \(architecture\)") and [town halls](/wiki/Ratusz "Ratusz").[363] [Cloth hall markets](/wiki/Cloth_hall "Cloth hall") ( _sukiennice_ ) were once an abundant feature of Polish urban architecture.[364] The mountainous south is known for its [Zakopane chalet style](/wiki/Zakopane_Style "Zakopane Style"), which originated in Poland.[365]

The earliest architectonic trend was [Romanesque](/wiki/Romanesque_architecture "Romanesque architecture") (c. 11th century), but its traces in the form of [circular rotundas](/wiki/Rotunda_\(architecture\) "Rotunda \(architecture\)") are scarce.[366] The arrival of [brick Gothic](/wiki/Brick_Gothic "Brick Gothic") (c. 13th century) defined Poland's most distinguishable medieval style, exuded by the castles of [Malbork](/wiki/Malbork_Castle "Malbork Castle"), [Lidzbark](/wiki/Lidzbark_Castle "Lidzbark Castle"), [Gniew](/wiki/Gniew_Castle "Gniew Castle") and [Kwidzyn](/wiki/Kwidzyn_Castle "Kwidzyn Castle") as well as the cathedrals of [Gniezno](/wiki/Gniezno_Cathedral "Gniezno Cathedral"), [Gdańsk](/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Church,_Gda%C5%84sk "St. Mary's Church, Gdańsk"), [Wrocław](/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw_Cathedral "Wrocław Cathedral"), [Frombork](/wiki/Frombork_Cathedral "Frombork Cathedral") and [Kraków](/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Basilica,_Krak%C3%B3w "St. Mary's Basilica, Kraków").[367] The [Renaissance](/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland "Renaissance in Poland") (16th century) gave rise to Italianate courtyards, defensive [palazzos](/wiki/Palazzo "Palazzo") and [mausoleums](/wiki/Sigismund%27s_Chapel "Sigismund's Chapel").[368] Decorative [attics](/wiki/Attic_\(architecture\) "Attic \(architecture\)") with [pinnacles](/wiki/Pinnacle "Pinnacle") and [arcade](/wiki/Arcade_\(architecture\) "Arcade \(architecture\)") [loggias](/wiki/Loggia "Loggia") are elements of [Polish Mannerism](/wiki/Mannerist_architecture "Mannerist architecture"), found in [Poznań](/wiki/Pozna%C5%84 "Poznań"), [Lublin](/wiki/Lublin "Lublin") and [Zamość](/wiki/Zamo%C5%9B%C4%87 "Zamość").[369][370] Foreign artisans often came at the expense of kings or nobles, whose palaces were built thereafter in the [Baroque](/wiki/Baroque_in_Poland "Baroque in Poland"), [Neoclassical](/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture_in_Poland "Neoclassical architecture in Poland") and [Revivalist](/wiki/Revivalism_\(architecture\) "Revivalism \(architecture\)") styles (17th–19th century).[371]

Primary building materials comprising [timber](/wiki/Lumber "Lumber") or [red brick](/wiki/Brick "Brick") were extensively utilised in Polish folk architecture,[372] and the concept of a [fortified church](/wiki/Fortified_church "Fortified church") was commonplace.[373] Secular structures such as [_dworek_ manor houses](/wiki/Dw%C3%B3r_\(manor_house\) "Dwór \(manor house\)"), [farmsteads](/wiki/Farmhouses "Farmhouses"), [granaries](/wiki/Granary "Granary"), [mills](/wiki/Gristmill "Gristmill") and country [inns](/wiki/Inn "Inn") are still present in some regions or in open air museums ( _[skansen](/wiki/Open-Air_Museum "Open-Air Museum")_ ).[374] However, traditional construction methods faded in the early-mid 20th century due to [urbanisation](/wiki/Urbanisation "Urbanisation") and the construction of [functionalist](/wiki/Functionalist_architecture "Functionalist architecture") [housing estates](/wiki/Housing_estate "Housing estate") and [residential areas](/wiki/Residential_architecture_in_Poland "Residential architecture in Poland").[375]

### Literature

Main articles: [Polish literature](/wiki/Polish_literature "Polish literature") and [History of philosophy in Poland](/wiki/History_of_philosophy_in_Poland "History of philosophy in Poland")

[![Adam Mickiewicz](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Wa%C5%84kowicz_Adam_Mickiewicz.jpg/154px-Wa%C5%84kowicz_Adam_Mickiewicz.jpg)](/wiki/File:Wa%C5%84kowicz_Adam_Mickiewicz.jpg)

[Adam Mickiewicz](/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz "Adam Mickiewicz"), whose [national epic poem](/wiki/Epic_poetry "Epic poetry") _[Pan Tadeusz](/wiki/Pan_Tadeusz "Pan Tadeusz")_ (1834) is considered a masterpiece of [Polish literature](/wiki/Polish_literature "Polish literature")

[![Joseph Conrad-Korzeniowski](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Joseph_Conrad%2C_Fotografie_von_George_Charles_Beresford%2C_1904.jpg/138px-Joseph_Conrad%2C_Fotografie_von_George_Charles_Beresford%2C_1904.jpg)](/wiki/File:Joseph_Conrad,_Fotografie_von_George_Charles_Beresford,_1904.jpg)

[Joseph Conrad](/wiki/Joseph_Conrad "Joseph Conrad"), author of popular books such as _[Heart of Darkness](/wiki/Heart_of_Darkness "Heart of Darkness")_ (1899) and _[Nostromo](/wiki/Nostromo "Nostromo")_ (1904)

The [literary works of Poland](/wiki/Polish_literature "Polish literature") have traditionally concentrated around the themes of [patriotism](/wiki/Patriotism "Patriotism"), [spirituality](/wiki/Spirituality "Spirituality"), social [allegories](/wiki/Allegory "Allegory") and [moral](/wiki/Moral "Moral") narratives.[376] The earliest examples of Polish literature, written in [Latin](/wiki/Latin "Latin"), date to the 12th century.[377] The first [Polish](/wiki/Polish_language "Polish language") phrase _Day ut ia pobrusa, a ti poziwai_ (officially translated as "Let me, I shall grind, and you take a rest") was documented in the [Book of Henryków](/wiki/Book_of_Henryk%C3%B3w "Book of Henryków") and reflected the use of a [quern-stone](/wiki/Quern-stone "Quern-stone").[378] It has been since included in [UNESCO's Memory of World Register](/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme "Memory of the World Programme").[379] The oldest extant manuscripts of fine [prose](/wiki/Prose "Prose") in [Old Polish](/wiki/Old_Polish_language "Old Polish language") are the [Holy Cross Sermons](/wiki/Holy_Cross_Sermons "Holy Cross Sermons") and the [Bible of Queen Sophia](/wiki/Bible_of_Queen_Sophia "Bible of Queen Sophia"),[380] and [Calendarium cracoviense](/wiki/Almanach_cracoviense_ad_annum_1474 "Almanach cracoviense ad annum 1474") (1474) is Poland's oldest surviving [print](/wiki/Printing_press "Printing press").[381]

The poets [Jan Kochanowski](/wiki/Jan_Kochanowski "Jan Kochanowski") and [Nicholas Rey](/wiki/Nicholas_Rey "Nicholas Rey") became the first [Renaissance](/wiki/Renaissance_in_Poland "Renaissance in Poland") authors to write in Polish.[382] Prime literarians of the period included [Dantiscus](/wiki/Johannes_Dantiscus "Johannes Dantiscus"), [Modrevius](/wiki/Andreus_Fricius_Modrevius "Andreus Fricius Modrevius"), [Goslicius](/wiki/Wawrzyniec_Go%C5%9Blicki "Wawrzyniec Goślicki"), [Sarbievius](/wiki/Matthias_Sarbievius "Matthias Sarbievius") and theologian [John Laski](/wiki/John_Laski "John Laski"). In the [Baroque](/wiki/Polish_Baroque "Polish Baroque") era, [Jesuit philosophy](/wiki/Jesuits "Jesuits") and local culture greatly influenced the literary techniques of [Jan Andrzej Morsztyn](/wiki/Jan_Andrzej_Morsztyn "Jan Andrzej Morsztyn") ([Marinism](/wiki/Marinism "Marinism")) and [Jan Chryzostom Pasek](/wiki/Jan_Chryzostom_Pasek "Jan Chryzostom Pasek") ([sarmatian](/wiki/Sarmatism "Sarmatism") memoirs).[383] During the [Enlightenment](/wiki/Polish_Enlightenment "Polish Enlightenment"), playwright [Ignacy Krasicki](/wiki/Ignacy_Krasicki "Ignacy Krasicki") composed the first Polish-language [novel](/wiki/The_Adventures_of_Mr._Nicholas_Wisdom "The Adventures of Mr. Nicholas Wisdom").[384] Poland's leading 19th-century [romantic poets](/wiki/Romanticism_in_Poland "Romanticism in Poland") were the [Three Bards](/wiki/Three_Bards "Three Bards") – [Juliusz Słowacki](/wiki/Juliusz_S%C5%82owacki "Juliusz Słowacki"), [Zygmunt Krasiński](/wiki/Zygmunt_Krasi%C5%84ski "Zygmunt Krasiński") and [Adam Mickiewicz](/wiki/Adam_Mickiewicz "Adam Mickiewicz"), whose epic poem _[Pan Tadeusz](/wiki/Pan_Tadeusz "Pan Tadeusz")_ (1834) is a national classic.[385] In the 20th century, the English [impressionist](/wiki/Impressionism_\(literature\) "Impressionism \(literature\)") and early [modernist](/wiki/Literary_modernism "Literary modernism") writings of [Joseph Conrad](/wiki/Joseph_Conrad "Joseph Conrad") made him one of the most eminent novelists of all time.[386][387]

Contemporary Polish literature is versatile, with its [fantasy](/wiki/Fantasy_literature "Fantasy literature") genre having been particularly praised.[388] The philosophical [sci-fi](/wiki/Science-fiction "Science-fiction") novel _[Solaris](/wiki/Solaris_\(novel\) "Solaris \(novel\)")_ by [Stanisław Lem](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Lem "Stanisław Lem") and _[The Witcher](/wiki/The_Witcher "The Witcher")_ series by [Andrzej Sapkowski](/wiki/Andrzej_Sapkowski "Andrzej Sapkowski") are celebrated works of world fiction.[389] Poland has six [Nobel-Prize winning](/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature "Nobel Prize in Literature") authors – [Henryk Sienkiewicz](/wiki/Henryk_Sienkiewicz "Henryk Sienkiewicz") ( _[Quo Vadis](/wiki/Quo_Vadis_\(novel\) "Quo Vadis \(novel\)")_ ; 1905), [Władysław Reymont](/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Reymont "Władysław Reymont") ( _[The Peasants](/wiki/The_Peasants "The Peasants")_ ; 1924), [Isaac Bashevis Singer](/wiki/Isaac_Bashevis_Singer "Isaac Bashevis Singer") (1978), [Czesław Miłosz](/wiki/Czes%C5%82aw_Mi%C5%82osz "Czesław Miłosz") (1980), [Wisława Szymborska](/wiki/Wis%C5%82awa_Szymborska "Wisława Szymborska") (1996), and [Olga Tokarczuk](/wiki/Olga_Tokarczuk "Olga Tokarczuk") (2018).[390][391][392]

### Cuisine

Main article: [Polish cuisine](/wiki/Polish_cuisine "Polish cuisine")

Selection of popular traditional dishes from Poland, including [hunter's stew](/wiki/Bigos "Bigos"), [stuffed cabbage rolls](/wiki/Go%C5%82%C4%85bki "Gołąbki"), [rye soup](/wiki/%C5%BBurek "Żurek"), [pierogi](/wiki/Pierogi "Pierogi"), [potato pancakes](/wiki/Potato_pancakes "Potato pancakes"), and [rye bread](/wiki/Rye_bread "Rye bread")

The cuisine of Poland is eclectic and shares similarities with other regional cuisines. Among the staple or regional dishes are [pierogi](/wiki/Pierogi "Pierogi") (filled dumplings), [kielbasa](/wiki/Kielbasa "Kielbasa") (sausage), [bigos](/wiki/Bigos "Bigos") (hunter's stew), [kotlet schabowy](/wiki/Kotlet_schabowy "Kotlet schabowy") (breaded cutlet), [gołąbki](/wiki/Go%C5%82%C4%85bki "Gołąbki") (cabbage rolls), [barszcz](/wiki/Borscht "Borscht") (borscht), [żurek](/wiki/%C5%BBurek "Żurek") (soured rye soup), [oscypek](/wiki/Oscypek "Oscypek") (smoked cheese), and [tomato soup](/wiki/Tomato_soup "Tomato soup").[393][394] [Bagels](/wiki/Bagel "Bagel"), a type of [bread roll](/wiki/Bread_roll "Bread roll"), also originated in Poland.[395]

Traditional dishes are hearty and abundant in [pork](/wiki/Pork "Pork"), potatoes, eggs, cream, mushrooms, regional herbs, and sauce.[396] Polish food is characteristic for its various kinds of [kluski](/wiki/Kluski "Kluski") (soft dumplings), [soups](/wiki/Soup "Soup"), [cereals](/wiki/Cereal "Cereal") and a variety of [breads](/wiki/Bread "Bread") and [open sandwiches](/wiki/Open_sandwich "Open sandwich"). Salads, including [mizeria](/wiki/Mizeria "Mizeria") (cucumber salad), [coleslaw](/wiki/Coleslaw "Coleslaw"), [sauerkraut](/wiki/Sauerkraut "Sauerkraut"), [carrot](/wiki/Carrot "Carrot") and [seared beets](/wiki/Searing "Searing"), are common. Meals conclude with a dessert such as [sernik](/wiki/Cheesecake "Cheesecake") (cheesecake), [makowiec](/wiki/Makowiec_\(pastry\) "Makowiec \(pastry\)") (poppy seed roll), or [napoleonka](/wiki/Napoleonka "Napoleonka") ([mille-feuille](/wiki/Mille-feuille "Mille-feuille")) cream pie.[397]

Traditional alcoholic beverages include honey [mead](/wiki/Mead_in_Poland "Mead in Poland"), widespread since the 13th century, [beer](/wiki/Beer_in_Poland "Beer in Poland"), wine and [vodka](/wiki/Vodka "Vodka").[398] The world's first written mention of vodka originates from Poland.[399] The most popular alcoholic drinks at present are beer and wine which took over from vodka more popular in the years 1980–1998.[400] [Grodziskie](/wiki/Grodziskie "Grodziskie"), sometimes referred to as "Polish Champagne", is an example of a historical beer style from Poland.[401] [Tea](/wiki/Tea "Tea") remains common in Polish society since the 19th century, whilst [coffee](/wiki/Coffee "Coffee") is drunk widely since the 18th century.[402]

### Fashion and design

Further information: [Category:Polish fashion](/wiki/Category:Polish_fashion "Category:Polish fashion")

Traditional _[polonaise](/wiki/Polonaise_\(clothing\) "Polonaise \(clothing\)")_ dresses, 1780–1785

Several Polish designers and stylists left a legacy of beauty inventions and [cosmetics](/wiki/Cosmetics "Cosmetics"); including [Helena Rubinstein](/wiki/Helena_Rubinstein "Helena Rubinstein") and [Maksymilian Faktorowicz](/wiki/Maksymilian_Faktorowicz "Maksymilian Faktorowicz"), who created a line of cosmetics company in [California](/wiki/California "California") known as [Max Factor](/wiki/Max_Factor "Max Factor") and formulated the term "make-up" which is now widely used as an alternative for describing cosmetics.[403] Faktorowicz is also credited with inventing modern [eyelash extensions](/wiki/Eyelash_extensions "Eyelash extensions").[404][405] As of 2020, Poland possesses the fifth-largest cosmetic market in Europe.[406] [Inglot Cosmetics](/wiki/Inglot_Cosmetics "Inglot Cosmetics") is the country's largest beauty products manufacturer,[407] and the retail store [Reserved](/wiki/Reserved "Reserved") is the country's most successful clothing store chain.[408]

Historically, [fashion](/wiki/Fashion "Fashion") has been an important aspect of Poland's national consciousness or [cultural manifestation](/wiki/Culture_of_Poland "Culture of Poland"), and the country developed its own style known as [Sarmatism](/wiki/Sarmatism "Sarmatism") at the turn of the 17th century.[409] The national dress and etiquette of Poland also reached the court at [Versailles](/wiki/Versailles "Versailles"), where French dresses inspired by Polish garments included _[robe à la polonaise](/wiki/Polonaise_\(clothing\) "Polonaise \(clothing\)")_ and the [witzchoura](/wiki/Witzchoura "Witzchoura"). The scope of influence also entailed furniture; rococo [Polish beds](/wiki/Polish_bed "Polish bed") with [canopies](/wiki/Canopy_bed "Canopy bed") became fashionable in French châteaus.[410] Sarmatism eventually faded in the wake of the 18th century.[409]

### Cinema

Main article: [Cinema of Poland](/wiki/Cinema_of_Poland "Cinema of Poland")

[Andrzej Wajda](/wiki/Andrzej_Wajda "Andrzej Wajda"), the recipient of an [Honorary Oscar](/wiki/Honorary_Oscar "Honorary Oscar"), the [Palme d'Or](/wiki/Palme_d%27Or "Palme d'Or"), as well as Honorary [Golden Lion](/wiki/Golden_Lion "Golden Lion") and [Golden Bear](/wiki/Golden_Bear "Golden Bear") awards

The [cinema of Poland](/wiki/Cinema_of_Poland "Cinema of Poland") traces its origins to 1894, when inventor [Kazimierz Prószyński](/wiki/Kazimierz_Pr%C3%B3szy%C5%84ski "Kazimierz Prószyński") patented the [Pleograph](/wiki/Pleograph "Pleograph") and subsequently the [Aeroscope](/wiki/Aeroscope "Aeroscope"), the first successful hand-held operated film camera.[411][412] In 1897, [Jan Szczepanik](/wiki/Jan_Szczepanik "Jan Szczepanik") constructed the [Telectroscope](/wiki/Telectroscope "Telectroscope"), a prototype of [television](/wiki/Color#Television "Color") transmitting images and sounds.[411] They are both recognised as pioneers of [cinematography](/wiki/Cinematography "Cinematography").[411] Poland has also produced influential directors, film producers and actors, many of whom were active in [Hollywood](/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles"), chiefly [Roman Polański](/wiki/Roman_Pola%C5%84ski "Roman Polański"), [Andrzej Wajda](/wiki/Andrzej_Wajda "Andrzej Wajda"), [Pola Negri](/wiki/Pola_Negri "Pola Negri"), [Samuel Goldwyn](/wiki/Samuel_Goldwyn "Samuel Goldwyn"), the [Warner brothers](/wiki/Warner_Brothers "Warner Brothers"), [Max Fleischer](/wiki/Max_Fleischer "Max Fleischer"), [Agnieszka Holland](/wiki/Agnieszka_Holland "Agnieszka Holland"), [Krzysztof Zanussi](/wiki/Krzysztof_Zanussi "Krzysztof Zanussi") and [Krzysztof Kieślowski](/wiki/Krzysztof_Kie%C5%9Blowski "Krzysztof Kieślowski").[413]

The [themes](/wiki/Film_genre "Film genre") commonly explored in Polish cinema include [history](/wiki/Historical_film "Historical film"), [drama](/wiki/Drama_\(film_and_television\) "Drama \(film and television\)"), war, culture and black realism ([film noir](/wiki/Film_noir "Film noir")).[411][412] In the 21st-century, two Polish productions won the [Academy Awards](/wiki/Academy_Awards "Academy Awards") – _[The Pianist](/wiki/The_Pianist_\(2002_film\) "The Pianist \(2002 film\)")_ (2002) by Roman Polański and _[Ida](/wiki/Ida_\(film\) "Ida \(film\)")_ (2013) by [Paweł Pawlikowski](/wiki/Pawe%C5%82_Pawlikowski "Paweł Pawlikowski").[412] Polish cinematography also created many well-received comedies. The most known of them were made by [Stanisław Bareja](/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Bareja "Stanisław Bareja") and [Juliusz Machulski](/wiki/Juliusz_Machulski "Juliusz Machulski"). 

### Media

Main articles: [Television in Poland](/wiki/Television_in_Poland "Television in Poland") and [Media of Poland](/wiki/Media_of_Poland "Media of Poland")

Further information: [Video games in Poland](/wiki/Video_games_in_Poland "Video games in Poland")

Headquarters of the publicly funded national television network [TVP](/wiki/Telewizja_Polska "Telewizja Polska") in Warsaw

According to the [Eurobarometer Report](/wiki/Eurobarometer "Eurobarometer") (2015), 78 percent of Poles watch the [television](/wiki/Television_in_Poland "Television in Poland") daily.[414] In 2020, 79 percent of the population read the news more than once a day, placing it second behind Sweden.[415] Poland has a number of major domestic media outlets, chiefly the [public broadcasting](/wiki/Public_broadcasting "Public broadcasting") corporation [TVP](/wiki/Telewizja_Polska "Telewizja Polska"), [free-to-air](/wiki/Free-to-air "Free-to-air") channels [TVN](/wiki/TVN_\(Polish_TV_channel\) "TVN \(Polish TV channel\)") and [Polsat](/wiki/Polsat "Polsat") as well as 24-hour news channels [TVP Info](/wiki/TVP_Info "TVP Info"), [TVN 24](/wiki/TVN_24 "TVN 24") and [Polsat News](/wiki/Polsat_News "Polsat News").[416] Public television extends its operations to genre-specific programmes such as [TVP Sport](/wiki/TVP_Sport "TVP Sport"), [TVP Historia](/wiki/TVP_Historia "TVP Historia"), [TVP Kultura](/wiki/TVP_Kultura "TVP Kultura"), [TVP Rozrywka](/wiki/TVP_Rozrywka "TVP Rozrywka"), TVP Seriale and [TVP Polonia](/wiki/TVP_Polonia "TVP Polonia"), the latter a state-run channel dedicated to the transmission of Polish-language telecasts for the [Polish diaspora](/wiki/Polish_diaspora "Polish diaspora"). In 2020, the most popular types of newspapers were [tabloids](/wiki/Tabloid_\(newspaper_format\) "Tabloid \(newspaper format\)") and socio-political news dailies.[414]

Poland is a major European hub for video game developers and among the most successful companies are [CD Projekt](/wiki/CD_Projekt "CD Projekt"), [Techland](/wiki/Techland "Techland"), [The Farm 51](/wiki/The_Farm_51 "The Farm 51"), [CI Games](/wiki/CI_Games "CI Games") and [People Can Fly](/wiki/People_Can_Fly "People Can Fly").[417] Some of the popular video games developed in Poland include [The Witcher](/wiki/The_Witcher_\(video_game_series\) "The Witcher \(video game series\)") trilogy and [Cyberpunk 2077](/wiki/Cyberpunk_2077 "Cyberpunk 2077").[417] The Polish city of [Katowice](/wiki/Katowice "Katowice") also hosts [Intel Extreme Masters](/wiki/Intel_Extreme_Masters "Intel Extreme Masters"), one of the biggest [esports](/wiki/Esports "Esports") events in the world.[417]

### Sports

Main articles: [Sport in Poland](/wiki/Sport_in_Poland "Sport in Poland") and [Poland at the Olympics](/wiki/Poland_at_the_Olympics "Poland at the Olympics")

The [Stadion Narodowy](/wiki/Stadion_Narodowy "Stadion Narodowy") in Warsaw, home of the [national football team](/wiki/Poland_national_football_team "Poland national football team")

[Motorcycle Speedway](/wiki/Motorcycle_Speedway "Motorcycle Speedway"), [volleyball](/wiki/Volleyball "Volleyball") and [association football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") are among the country's most popular sports, with a rich history of international competitions.[418][419] [Track and field](/wiki/Track_and_field_athletics "Track and field athletics"), [basketball](/wiki/Basketball "Basketball"), [handball](/wiki/Handball "Handball"), boxing, [MMA](/wiki/Mixed_martial_arts "Mixed martial arts"), [ski jumping](/wiki/Ski_jumping "Ski jumping"), [cross-country skiing](/wiki/Cross-country_skiing_\(sport\) "Cross-country skiing \(sport\)"), [ice hockey](/wiki/Ice_hockey "Ice hockey"), tennis, fencing, swimming, and [weightlifting](/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting "Olympic weightlifting") are other popular sports. The golden era of [football in Poland](/wiki/Football_in_Poland "Football in Poland") occurred throughout the 1970s and went on until the early 1980s when the [Polish national football team](/wiki/Poland_national_football_team "Poland national football team") achieved their best results in any FIFA World Cup competitions finishing third place in [the 1974](/wiki/1974_FIFA_World_Cup "1974 FIFA World Cup") and [the 1982](/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup "1982 FIFA World Cup") tournaments. The team won a gold medal [in football](/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics "Football at the Summer Olympics") at the [1972 Summer Olympics](/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics "1972 Summer Olympics") and two silver medals, [in 1976](/wiki/1976_Summer_Olympics "1976 Summer Olympics") and [in 1992](/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics "1992 Summer Olympics"). In 2012, Poland co-hosted the [UEFA European Football Championship](/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012 "UEFA Euro 2012").[420]

As of August 2023, the [Polish men's national volleyball team](/wiki/Poland_men%27s_national_volleyball_team "Poland men's national volleyball team") is ranked [as first](/wiki/FIVB_World_Rankings "FIVB World Rankings") in the world.[421] The team won a gold medal at the [1976 Summer Olympics](/wiki/Volleyball_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament "Volleyball at the 1976 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament") and the gold medal at the [FIVB World Championship](/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship "FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship") [1974](/wiki/1974_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship "1974 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship"), [2014](/wiki/2014_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship "2014 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship") and [2018](/wiki/2018_FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_World_Championship "2018 FIVB Volleyball Men's World Championship").[422][423] [Mariusz Pudzianowski](/wiki/Mariusz_Pudzianowski "Mariusz Pudzianowski") is a highly successful strongman competitor and has won more [World's Strongest Man](/wiki/World%27s_Strongest_Man "World's Strongest Man") titles than any other competitor in the world, winning the event in 2008 for the fifth time.[424]

Poland has made a distinctive mark [in motorcycle speedway racing](/wiki/Speedway_in_Poland "Speedway in Poland"). The top [Ekstraliga](/wiki/Speedway_Ekstraliga "Speedway Ekstraliga") division has one of [the highest average attendances](/wiki/List_of_attendance_figures_at_domestic_professional_sports_leagues#Outdoor_sports "List of attendance figures at domestic professional sports leagues") for any sport in Poland. The [national speedway team of Poland](/wiki/Poland_national_speedway_team "Poland national speedway team") is one of the major teams in international speedway. Individually, Poland has three [Speedway Grand Prix](/wiki/Speedway_Grand_Prix "Speedway Grand Prix") World Champions, with the most successful being three-time World Champion [Bartosz Zmarzlik](/wiki/Bartosz_Zmarzlik "Bartosz Zmarzlik") who won back-to-back championships in 2019 and 2020 as well as 2022 and 2023. In 2021, Poland finished runners-up in the Speedway of Nations world championship final, held in Manchester, UK in 2021.[425]

In the 21st century, the country has seen a growth of popularity of [tennis](/wiki/Tennis "Tennis") and produced a number of successful tennis players including World No. 1 [Iga Świątek](/wiki/Iga_%C5%9Awi%C4%85tek "Iga Świątek"), winner of four [Grand Slam](/wiki/Grand_Slam_\(tennis\) "Grand Slam \(tennis\)") singles titles; former World No. 2 [Agnieszka Radwanska](/wiki/Agnieszka_Radwanska "Agnieszka Radwanska"), winner of 20 WTA career singles titles including [2015 WTA Finals](/wiki/2015_WTA_Finals_%E2%80%93_Singles "2015 WTA Finals – Singles"); Top 10 ATP player [Hubert Hurkacz](/wiki/Hubert_Hurkacz "Hubert Hurkacz"); and former World No. 1 doubles player [Łukasz Kubot](/wiki/%C5%81ukasz_Kubot "Łukasz Kubot") whose career highlights include winning two Grand Slam doubles titles – [2014 Australian Open](/wiki/2014_Australian_Open_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_doubles "2014 Australian Open – Men's doubles") and [2017 Wimbledon Championships](/wiki/2017_Wimbledon_Championships_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_doubles "2017 Wimbledon Championships – Men's doubles"). Poland also won the [2015 Hopman Cup](/wiki/2015_Hopman_Cup "2015 Hopman Cup") with Agnieszka Radwańska and [Jerzy Janowicz](/wiki/Jerzy_Janowicz "Jerzy Janowicz") representing the country.[426][427]

Poles made significant achievements in mountaineering, in particular, in the [Himalayas](/wiki/Himalayas "Himalayas") and the winter ascending of the [eight-thousanders](/wiki/Eight-thousander "Eight-thousander"). Polish mountains are one of the tourist attractions of the country. Hiking, climbing, skiing and mountain biking and attract numerous tourists every year from all over the world.[266] Water sports are the most popular summer recreation activities, with ample locations for fishing, canoeing, kayaking, sailing and windsurfing especially in the northern regions of the country.[428]

United Kingdom| 

  * [England](/wiki/England "England")
  * [Scotland](/wiki/Scotland "Scotland")
  * [Wales](/wiki/Wales "Wales")
  * [Northern Ireland](/wiki/Northern_Ireland "Northern Ireland") ([country of the United Kingdom](/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom "Countries of the United Kingdom") subject to the [British-Irish Agreement](/wiki/Good_Friday_Agreement "Good Friday Agreement"))

  
  
  * 1 Spans the conventional boundary between Europe and another continent.
  * 2 Considered European for cultural, political and historical reasons but is geographically in Western Asia.
  * 3 [Oceanic islands](/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands "Island") within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.
  * 4 Governed by the [Holy See](/wiki/Holy_See "Holy See") which has sovereignty over Vatican City.
